O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	Oh you, my dear son, I have completed for you this book, which is the culmination of the science of medicine together with its full content, and I have brought it to an end with its explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is a part of manual work, that is, "surgery."
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the manual work has been neglected in our region and has disappeared altogether, the science is thus lost and fragmented, with nothing left of it except small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which time has altered.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this have come errors and vanities, intentions are obscured, and science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I want to revive it along with the organization of this treatise according to the path of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will include the forms of the cautery tools and of the other instruments of the work, along with added explanations and preparations, as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And due to the fact that no good master of manual skills is found in our time, the art of medicine is diminished.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is fitting that whoever undertakes this work should excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the limbs, their forms, connections, and separations, and has knowledge of the bones, nerves, and muscles, the number of bones, and the movement of moving and resting veins, and where they arise.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason Hippocrates says that "name with name is much, and with work is little"; and especially in the art of manual skill.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say to you at the start of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable of the aforementioned matters should guard against falling into error and killing people, as I have seen many times with those who engage in this science and yet go about it without knowledge or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish doctor who cut an abscess of scrofula on a woman’s neck, and he cut the arteries of the neck; so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another doctor who extracted a stone from an elderly man, and the stone was large; he took with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to remove it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if it were removed, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another doctor who took into his care a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and this doctor, full of ignorance, tightly bandaged the break with splints on top of the wound, leaving no ventilation for the wound, and left it like this for a time; he told him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg and foot were entirely swollen and began to deteriorate.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hastened to come and unbind the leg; and when I untied it, he felt at peace and no pain at all.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But even so, the corruption was already established in the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not stop spreading through the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another doctor who incised a cancerous ulcer, and then inflamed it by his lack of skill.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on il touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a cancer, when it is pure from melancholic humor, it should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place where all the corrupted part can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dearest son, it is necessary that you know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, work where there is danger in several conditions; and I will show in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos. Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Therefore, it is necessary that you take care, so that foolish doctors cannot speak ill of you. So take up your tools with skill, and treat your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best approach so that by the grace of God you may bring them to health and be praised; and leave aside dreadful diseases of severe severity; and put away your tools from what causes you to doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may pass from this world to the next in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen says in some of his warnings: "Do not take on an incurable disease, lest you be called a foolish doctor."
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have arranged this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et de cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cautery with fire and sharp medicinal cauteries, and the chapter is organized from head to foot; and about the forms of instruments and the cautery tools, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cupping, wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapter is organized with the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about setting dislocations and twisting, and similar things; and it is organized from head to foot, with the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we recall the work, it is fitting that I speak of the quality of the aid and of the harm for each constitution.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and of harm are the longest discourse and the most subtle science, and the concealed secret; and on this many wise men have spoken, and agreed on it; but I am satisfied with few of their words, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cautery universally aids every constitution where there is matter, except for two constitutions: namely, a hot constitution without matter, and a dry constitution without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a hot and dry constitution together with matter, some stated and said that cautery is a great aid; and others said the opposite: that cautery is not useful for an illness that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and a hot illness should not be cured by heat, nor by dryness; and the one who says otherwise says that cautery gives great aid to hot and dry illnesses that come in people’s bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it sometimes through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And still, let no one undertake this except he who has experienced it, and who knows through long practice the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of people’s constitutions, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and the passage of time; we have no fear of the other constitutions, especially in cold and moist illnesses.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all doctors came together and agreed upon cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that cautery together with fire is among the secrets of cures, and of greater virtue than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it affects only the member that is burned, and does little harm to any other member.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide. Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines pass from one member to another as they spread, and they bring to the member grievous diseases of difficult cure; and by chance they may kill the patient. Fire, due to its nobility and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless there is an excess of it.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this through experiment and through the long service and study I have devoted to the art, based on the truth of things; and thus I excuse myself for the length of this discussion, as it does not please me to deprive you of the secret that is revealed in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives out diseases from the body, as the philosopher has said in demonstration; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they agreed upon the time when cauteries should be done, and they chose spring.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cautery is appropriate in all seasons, because the arising harm is mitigated with the aid of cautery; and especially if the cautery is for urgent pains which cannot wait for the season lest greater harm come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think about this, dear son, in the way foolish doctors do; for the illness that is cured by cautery does not return at all; and they say this is so; but it is not as they think, because cautery is nothing other than a medicine that alters the constitution and dries the humors that are the cause of the pain, and is worth more than medicine due to the speed of its effect and the virtue of its work and its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it is possible that the illness sometimes returns according to the constitution of the patient and the place of the illness and its strength; and the excesses are accumulated in him through the acquisition of foods and similar things, unless it is cauteries administered in a place where there is little excess and moisture, as with tooth cautery for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cautery has worth after medicine, but their thinking is false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer various cures for an illness and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Thus it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not as foolish doctors understand it.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that a cautery of a gold instrument is better than one of iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; and they said that the place of the cautery does not cause rot, but this is not true for I have tested it, and have found that this is true in some men; and cautery with gold is worth more than with iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And yet when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly; and if it is heated too much, it deforms in the fire; and so there are enough hindrances with it.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use iron cautery, as we have prepared it much more for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have arranged this chapter for you from head to foot, so that the path may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	About the cautery of the olive.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is good for moisture and coldness in the brain, and there are two kinds performed due to an illness called "soda" and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for a multitude of dreams, toothache, sore throat, and especially for all illnesses that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a cleansing medicine for the head for three or four nights, according to what the strength, age, and condition of the patient can bear; and then shave the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then make him sit cross-legged with his hands on his chest; afterward, place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes, and where your middle fingers rest, mark there with ink, then heat the cautery called "olive," of which this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it on the spot marked with ink, descending and pressing your hand little by little while turning; then quickly lift your hand and inspect the spot to see if you glimpse the bone just a bit; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take a little salt, put it in water, moisten cotton with it, place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; after that, place cotton moistened with butter on it; and leave it until the burn is removed; afterward, treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients said that the longer the wound remains open, the more it purges; and this helps much.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And some said that one should leave the cautery in place until part of the bone is burnt, and then remove what is burnt from the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that one should leave the cautery in place and press so firmly that the bone is abraded as wide as a spindle whorl that women put on their spindles, so that the humors may flow out; and the wound should be left open for a long time; afterward, it should be cleaned and closed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good in every case, except in some men where there is a way to fear; and it seems to me that I should abandon it, for the head is weakened by continuous natural discharge, as we observe in other body parts; and especially when the patient's head is weak by nature, the first type of cautery is safer and better to me, and I use it with combined safety and health.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	On the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When chronic pain arises throughout the head and lasts a long time, the patient should use oils and pills called "cochie," along with head-cleansing and oils and plasters; and if the cautery we have previously mentioned is applied and is ineffective.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take note if the patient’s head is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize a little below the cautery we mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	Then apply cautery to each side of the head down to the bone, as we have said before, and apply a cautery at the spot called "vessels"; this is the place where cups are applied; and ease your hand so that you do not go to the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; it is necessary that the cautery of the sides be more subtle than that with which one cauterizes the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	On cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain arises in one part of the head and the illness extends to the eye, and the head has been purged by cleansing medicines, and all other treatments described in the division of illnesses have been done and none have helped, then apply cautery in two ways, namely with a sharp medicine and with iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cautery with sharp medicine is done by taking a clove of garlic, peeling it, and cutting a little off the two ends, then cutting open the temple where the pain is in such a way that you can place the garlic clove under the skin; when it is placed, bind and compress it well and leave it for twelve hours; then unbind it, remove the garlic clove, and leave the wound like that for two or three days; afterward, place cotton soaked in butter on it until the discharge comes out.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	Then treat it with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish, use one of the burning medicines I have described in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The cautery with iron is done in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery, which has the following form:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	It is called "claw" because the head is shaped like a nail with a slight curve, and in the middle there is a small protrusion; place it on the painful spot, hold your hand there, and turn the iron lightly until half the thickness of the flesh is burned; then lift your hand so as not to burn the artery, which lies underneath, and an abundance of blood will flow.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Afterward, place cotton soaked in salt water on the spot for three days; then place cotton soaked in butter, and then treat the spot with ointment until it is healed; and if you want, cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "knife-like," with its tip, and take care not to cut the artery in this migraine, which is not old.
de emigraine	On migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have described in the divisions of illnesses, and it does not help, and you see that the cauteries with medicine and with iron are insufficient, then you must heat the cautery called "knife-like" until it is white-hot; and first cut a line on the painful spot, half a finger in length, and lift your hand once, and compress it so that you do not cut the artery and do not reach the bone; be careful of the mandible that moves when one eats, and avoid the nerve so that the jaw is not affected and spasm does not come upon the patient, and be careful of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, as there is great fear in cutting it, especially for one who is not experienced or trained; and leave the procedure midway; but I will tell you how to stop the blood flow when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it applies in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this cautery is not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is enduring, cauterize the middle of the head as we have described, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, use the cautery we mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, along with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more effective.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	On ear pain due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When cold-induced pain comes to the ear, and solutions and other treatments we have mentioned in the division have been applied, and the pain does not subside, then heat the cautery called "point," which has the following form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then apply small points all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move a little above the base of the ear after marking the spot with ink; and make ten points around each ear; then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	On the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that should be cured by cautery is only that which arises from phlegm, as we have described in the divisions of illness; and do not use cautery on conditions that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this form of torture that comes from phlegm, using head purges and gargling, and these do not work, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another slightly above the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; place the cautery on the area that appears healthy, and apply cautery right at the top of the ear, slightly below the top of the head, and another on the temple about the length of a thumb; and leave the cautery on long enough so that half of the flesh is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it resembles the “knife-like” cautery we described above, but it is a little more delicate and the blade must be a little thicker; afterward, treat the spot as I previously described, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is longstanding and you treat it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then apply four cauteries: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one at the spot called the “vassel” as we mentioned before, and the last cautery above the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said above.
de litargie	For lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient strong purgatives and pills that cleanse the brain; afterwards, shave the entire head of the patient, and place on the occiput the mustard plaster that is described in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of the cautery: do it as I have described.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is healed thus, it is good; and if he is not, make him three cauteries from the middle of the head down to the neck, with a space between each cautery of two finger-widths; and treat him as with the others, and if you wish to add to this, and the patient can endure it, make one cautery in the center; and if needed, two more on the two sides, and treat him until he is healed; and let the cautery be the one called "olive-shaped," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	For coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleansed with purgatives and with what we have previously mentioned; afterwards, shave the patient’s head, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each side, one at the back and three along the spine of the neck; and if more is needed, if the body is moist and the patient endures it, and the disease is strong, make four cauteries along the spine of the back; leave it until the majority of the heart is burned, and lift your hand; afterwards, treat him until he is healed, and let the cautery be the one called "olive-shaped," as we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	For epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic must not make use of a cautery except if he is phlegmatic, and it is necessary first to cleanse the brain with purgatives and other treatments that we have stated in the section when the patient is older and able to tolerate medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot bear it, give him gargles and mouth treatments that cleanse the brain often along with good foods; then shave his head in the center, and make one cautery as we have described before, and one cautery on the vein, and on each side; and if the patient is strong and endures, make cauteries as I have described for one who has paralysis and weakness of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped in the manner I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, make one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, because of melancholy, there are excess fluids or corrupted moistures and thick phlegm, then cauterize with such cauteries as we have described for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, because of melancholy, the excess fluids are declining into melancholy, and the patient’s body is moist, then give him something to drink to cleanse his brain, as we previously described in the section.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, shave the head of the patient; then make a well-made linen pad, like a circle, and place it on the middle of the head; and let the patient be seated crosswise, and well held from all sides; then apply the dressing, using old sheep's butter; and heat it with a moderate fire, so that if one touches it with a finger, it can be endured; then empty the circle in the middle of the head, and let it cool; do this to the patient once a week, with other good management, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish, cauterize him by making several points with the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery gently moistens the brain; and then apply cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat.
de l’awe des eulz	For water in the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When water first comes to the eyes, according to the signs I mentioned in the section, then begin and give the patient something to drink that cleanses the head, and keep him from all moistures, and make him sweat or bathe several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	Then instruct him to tilt his head back, and make a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the flow of water affects both eyes, or one if it affects only one; and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries that are under the heart, and let the cautery be as long as the width of the temple; and beware of the flow of blood, and if you see too much blood flowing, then staunch it with whatever means you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will instruct you on the extraction of the arteries and the method of incision on how to staunch it; and sometimes one makes a cautery or incision below the two bones at the back.
dou cors des larmes	For the cause of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When tears in the eyes are old and chronic and are upon the veins, or near the arteries that are visible on the outside of the head; and it is seen that it is from cold, phlegmatic excesses, then make the cautery I mentioned at the beginning of the water descending to the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries on the back below the two bones; and if there is need for more, then cauterize wisely above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	For the cause of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the section, and it does not help, then give the patient to drink for three nights consecutively; afterwards, shave the head, and make a cautery in the middle with an olive-shaped cautery; and make two cauteries with the cautery called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, a little below the hair; and be careful not to cut the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the eyelid is softened from disease and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery that is called "olive-shaped."
de coi ci est li forme:	Of which this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you wish, make two cauteries on the two eyebrows as long as the brows are; and do not leave your hand there except long enough for a third part of the eyelid to be burned, in the manner I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	For the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are turned inward, and prick the eye, and cauteries are made in two manners: that is, by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	With the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are long and even; and if they prick him at their base, he should squeeze his eyes so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they have grown and are even, then place the patient at ease; then trace on the eyelid a shape like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the mark be beside the hairs; then apply cotton soaked in egg white and parsley juice on the eye, then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cauterize over the figure that you have marked little by little many times, so that the center is burned there; and the sign of successful work is that you see the eyelid retract, and the hairs lifted away from the point of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it like this for three days, then apply cotton soaked in butter until the scald is removed; then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if, after this, the hairs return, and the eyelid is softened, then redo the cautery on that same spot, as you did before; and if the hairs are misaligned, cauterize so that the eyelid rises to its natural position, is even, and the hairs no longer prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cautery of burning medicine is to instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are long and even, then make from parchment the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each weighing three grams, and grind them well together; do it quickly so it does not cool, then spread it on the form you made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the eyelid; if the illness affects only one eye, you should work on that one, or on both if needed; and place under the eye cotton moistened with egg white; the patient's head should be supported, and press with your finger on the medicine, pressing lightly and moving it whenever the patient feels the medicine sting, as it stings like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a while, remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the stinging has passed, wash the area with water, and observe if you see the eyelid raised as if it were lifted by the constraint of fire or incision; and if it is so, then it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, then apply more medicine to the area where it hasn’t worked, until your work is even and your eyes are correctly aligned; then apply cotton moistened with butter until the burned area has cooled, then treat the area with an ointment called “dyafenis” and another until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And it is necessary that you carefully guard your work so that none of the medicine falls into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the eyelid becomes soft afterward and the hairs prick the eye, then redo the medicine on the area where the eyelid has softened, just as you did before; then treat it until it is healed; and this is the shape of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that people’s eyes vary in size, whether large or small, and so your constraints should match accordingly; and let the correct path not be hidden from one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On treating fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the sections on diseases, and your treatments do not work, then it is necessary to make a cautery in this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head against you; and let an assistant hold his head between his hands in such a way that he does not move or turn his head; then place cotton moistened with egg white or parsley juice on the eye; then heat a cautery shaped thus: it is rounded at the head like the shape of a vulture’s feather, with the cautery in it; if you wish, let it be pointed from one end to the other, or if you wish, let it be like a tent; but in any case, this rounded form is best for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Then press the fistula if it is open, and extract the rot, and dry it; and if it is closed, open it, and draw out the matter; then place the cautery on it very hot, and hold your hand on the cautery over the clean part above the eye, so that your hand does not make an error; then place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and spoil it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you reach the beginning of the cauterization down to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors;  Aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then begin the cauterization again once more, and another time if needed, and leave it for three days. Afterward, place moist cotton soaked in butter over it, and treat it with drying ointment until it is healed, and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply a corrosive acidic medicine until the bone is exposed; and do this again according to what will follow in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a type of cauterization of fistula that some of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Pay attention to the fistula, and split the area; afterward, place a small camahan in the opening, which is made as follows:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil;  et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: the lead then burns the area of the fistula, and heals it with marvelous effectiveness.	make it to the size of a “.З.” of lead; and hold the camahan firmly in your hand, and make sure the patient doesn’t move at all, so that the molten lead doesn’t run into his eye; and it’s necessary to place on the patient’s eye cotton soaked in egg white or in water; li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, it’s necessary to administer piercings to the nose, and bring the fistula back to the body of the nose, as is required in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	Of cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often cracks appear on the lips that are called "poil," especially on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described in the incisions, and the treatment does not work, then heat a small knife cautery according to this method:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it quickly in these cracks until it reaches the bottom; afterward, treat the area with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	Of abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, it causes decay and breaks down, becoming foul and turning into a fistula; and you treat it as we have explained in previous sections, but it does not improve: then you must apply a cautery according to the size of the fistula; next, press it at the opening of the fistula, and keep your hand steady so that the hot iron reaches its base, and to the deepest part; and do this once or twice, then treat it with the remedies we have described, until it is healed; and if it heals in this way, that is good; but if not, it is necessary to expose the area and remove the decayed bone, as you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	Of the loosening of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth are loose, and you treat it with medicines and it does not work, then place the head of the patient on your lap; then heat the cautery, the shape of which will be given hereafter, in such a way that you place a cover over the tooth; and quickly place the hot cautery inside, and hold it so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and apply the cautery again as needed; afterward, have the patient fill his mouth with salt water, keep it for an hour, and spit it out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in such a manner the tooth that was loose is strengthened, the softened gums are firmed, and the spoiled moisture is dried.
de la dolor des dens	Of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When tooth pain arises from cold, or there is cold or dampness present, and medical treatments are ineffective, then a cautery is needed in two ways: a butter cautery and a fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	The butter cautery is done by taking cow butter, putting it in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton, wrap it around the tip of a tent, soak it in boiling butter, and place it quickly on the aching tooth, holding it there until it cools; do this repeatedly until the heat reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, soak wool and cotton in cold butter, place it on the aching tooth, and press a hot iron over it until the heat penetrates to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The fire cautery is done by taking an iron or bronze cover, thick enough so the heat does not reach the patient’s mouth; then heat the cautery, the form of which will be described later, place it on the tooth, and hold it until the cautery cools; do this often, as it will relieve the pain that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter as the cautery is applied, and then spit it out; and that is the method of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cautery of whichever type you wish, according to what you are able; and that is the method of the cover.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is from phlegm and cold moisture, and does not respond to medicinal digestion, then heat the cautery head, the form of which will be given hereafter, and make sure it has two openings for the fumes to escape through to the other side of the cautery; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it for three days; then apply butter-soaked cotton on it until the burn is gone; then treat the area with ointments and dressings until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cover:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture overcomes the channels of the lung, especially when it comes from a cold temperament, the patient must first be emptied with laxative medicines; then apply a cautery at the base of the throat, and be careful not to go all the way to the throat, and only burn a little, not deeply.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then make another cautery at the junction of the neck at the top of the spine, using the cautery called the "clavicle," the form of which we mentioned previously; and treat the area as we have previously described until it is healed.
de la toust	On cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When coughs and lung disease are caused by cold moistures, and the patient has no fever or dryness, and the illness is chronic, make two cauteries on the small muscles in open areas; and another cautery in the center of the chest between the two breasts; and let the cautery be called the “key” shape, according to the previously described form.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you wish, make a cautery in the style of the full “point” cautery, whose form was described above in the treatment for ear disease; and let the points be up to thirty, or around that number.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	Then treat the area as previously described, and let the cautery have three branches in this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the cauteries are lighter, since you make three at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	On dislocation of the joint
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the joint is dislocated due to moisture, and it is put back in place but cannot stay and instead keeps dislocating with even slight movement, as we have observed, then it is necessary that you first stabilize the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Then lay the patient on his back and on his side; next, raise the flesh inside the joint socket with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inwardly, heat the cautery that has two branches, for which the form is given here:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	And cauterize the heart until it is pierced to the ribs, and the shape of the cauterization will come with four cauters together; and for this, a cauterization is made with the cauter that has three nerves, by which the figure of cauterization is six cauters; and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent and this is the form of the cauter with three nerves:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes there is added on this a single nerve by which there are eight cauters.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	Then put on the cauter ground pearls with salt; then let the patient rest, and the limb should not be moved for a long time until it is well strengthened.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is loosened above, which rarely happens, then cauterize on the thickness of the clavicle cauter, or apply many pointed cauters.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come chills and much moisture such that they damage its temperament, and the catarrhs multiply there, and the usual cures do not help, then it is necessary that the patient lie on his back, and extend his legs and his hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	After this, make three cauters, one below the spoon of the chest to the size of a finger, with the clavicle cauter, and two cauters on the two sides so that the figure of the cauters forms three angles, with such space between them that they are not joined when they will emit putrefaction; and let the cauters be deep enough that they reach both parts of the heart, and the form of the cauters should be in this shape without addition:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cauter in the middle of the stomach in this shape; and for one who fears this cauter, cauterize by pricking and bleeding at a point on the stomach according to the amount you wish of the lance; then cauterize with the whole cauter which is called the “point.”
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then follow the treatment of the remedy that we mentioned earlier, until he is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When cold and moisture and thick windiness cause pain in the liver, until it is removed from its natural temperament by excess; and the patient is treated with the remedies we mentioned before, and it does not help, it is necessary that the patient lie on his back; then make three cauters with the lance in this shape, this figure, and this amount on the liver, outside the hypochondria, where the rib of the man is; and there should be a space between each cauter the width of a finger; and let the cauters be along the length of the body, and do not press too hard with the entire cauter; and only burn half of the heart, and let the patient be upright on his feet; and if he cannot, let him lie down, extend his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if it is your wish, cauterize these cauters with the small knife, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and take care not to burn the whole heart, for you would dry the whole body; and let it not come to a boil, for the heart is very delicate there, and know this as truth.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain, but not too intense; and if it is in the membrane, he feels raging pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this cure is advised by the physicians, it is necessary that the patient be laid on his head; and then bleed with the lance the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cauter which is similar to the ray, of which here is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with one cauter until the heart is burned, and it reaches the siphac, until the putrefaction is entirely removed; then treat according to the treatment of the abscesses until he is healed; and let no one use this cauter unless he has studied the art of medicine for a long time, and in whose hands these ailments have been cured more than once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may work boldly, and yet it seems to me that it is often better to leave it.
dou cautere de pleuresin	The cauterization for pleuresy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that for pleuresy one should make cauterizations with roots of aristolochia, and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find, let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your fingers; and soak it in oil, heat it in the fire, and cauterize one cauter between the pit and the neck, and two small cauters a little further down in the part below the beard; and two cauters between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclining a little backward; and one cauter in the middle of the chest, and one on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two on the two sides of the chest opposite the cauter between the two shoulders; and do not press hard with your hand, but rather make it as light as if you were smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancients said that some men use a cauter shaped like a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs, until it reaches the abscess; and the pain springs out, as we have said about the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this procedure there is danger that the patient may die immediately, or a fistula may form which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Of the spleen
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of the spleen with the cures we mentioned in the divisions, and it does not help, then there are three types of cauterization which are all good.
