Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of these, one method is to make three or four cauters, aligned along the length of the spleen, according to the shape of the liver cauter we mentioned before; and do not press hard with the cauter, and let the patient lie often on his back; and another type of cauterization is to heat the cauter which has two nerves, as we showed in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is near the spleen, where the patient’s rib extends toward the left, and let the elevation by which you lift the heart be in line with the heart, according to the length of the body, and let the cauters follow the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Then insert the two inflamed nerves until the heart is pierced on the other side, and then withdraw the cauter, and there will be four in this way. And if you wish, cauterize with the whole cauter with three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	Then follow the cure when it has expelled the decay for a long time, and this is often more effective than the other cures mentioned before.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not beneficial for dropsy, except in the way called “ascites.”
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we mentioned in the divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you make four cauters around the navel, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two on the back along the spine, and one near the chest; and let the cauters be very near the thickness of the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Then leave the cauter open to release putrefaction for a long time, and do not abandon the treatment of the patient after the cauterization; and the healing will be hastened, and the two intentions will be joined with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	Let the shape of the cauter for the abdomen be the clavicle type which we showed before; and the one for the back be olive-shaped, as it was indicated here above.
de l’enfleure des piez	Of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in someone who has dropsy and are full of yellowish water, you must cauterize on the top of the foot between the little toe and the ring toe; and lift your hand with the cauter without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go too deep, so that the yellowish water may drain out, and let the cauter be in this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Then make two cauters on each of the two legs at the point of the knife; and let the cauters be lengthwise, one below the knee in front and the other on the back, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauters open for a long time without treating them, so that the water may flow out; then treat with the other remedies we have mentioned.
de la menoison	Of dysentery
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When looseness of the bowels is caused by cold and moisture, such that the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and it cannot be cured by other remedies; and you see the patient in good spirits and of strong constitution, then make one large cauterization on the stomach as mentioned above in the stomach cauterization, in a circular cauterization; and four delicate cauters around the navel with one delicate clavicle cauter, and two cauters on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see moisture in abundance and the patient suffering, then make a cauter on the wrist, and one cauter on each armpit, and two small cauters on the stomach beside the large one, for the cure is effective when there is good support.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or several, and they are old and are from thick, cold, and moist corrupted humors, and they have been treated as we have mentioned in divisions, and it has not helped, then make cauterizations: three along the spine of the back, one directly below the coccyx in a triangle, and one cauter two finger-widths below the navel; and if you think his stomach is cold, and food does not digest, and the face swells, then make a large cauterization on the stomach as mentioned before, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen with the clavicle cauter; and leave the cauter open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of the fleshiness called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut the thelul, heat the cauter that resembles a razor, and then place it, fully red-hot, on the cut thelul; and leave your hand there until the cauter reaches the origin of the vein, where the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is much thelul, cauterize each one as we have said; afterward treat with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cauter on the alchatim, it will be of even greater help.
de plaie mal curee	Of poorly healed wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, such an illness comes that can only be healed by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When someone has a fistula that is old and discharges pus and corrupted moisture, you must probe it with a delicate probe, and ensure that you know with the probe how deep it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	Then heat the cauter that resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula to the depth that the probe entered, and reapply the cauter so that the rotten and corrupted tissue is burned away, once, twice, or three times, as necessary; and be careful not to burn the nerves nearby or the large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula reaches the body of the bladder and the intestine, then beware of these places, and do this only in a fleshy area, and remember it is not perforating; then treat the place until it is healed, and if the area is dry and the matter has been removed for a long time, then you know that the area is completely healed; and if the matter is not removed, know that the place is hollowed out, and the bone at the bottom is corrupted; as in one of those we will discuss in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When cold pain occurs in the kidneys, and with it a heavy flatulence, and there is no desire for women, then you must make cauterizations on each side of the kidneys with the clavicle cauter we mentioned earlier; and if we cauterize the middle, there will be three cauters in a line, which will be of even greater help.
de la vessie	Of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weakened from cold and moisture, such that the patient retains urine, then make a cauterization on the area above the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and one on the right and one on the left, and let each cauter be as long as a thumbnail; and make one cauter on the back, or two if needed; and let the cauter be clavicle-shaped as described earlier.
de la marris	Of the womb
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, and it nevertheless does not prevent conception, and the periods are corrupted and delayed; and when they come, there is great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauterizations around the belly, as we have said in the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations on the back; and let the cauterizations be of the nail-type, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistures descend to the joint of the hip, and as a result it shifts from its place, and the sign is that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the place of separation is found empty, so you must cauterize the patient above the hip joint with a circular cauterization, and bleed in front of the place around the joint as it turns, so that the joint is within the circle; and let the cauterization be like those used to cauterize the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you do not have this cauterization tool, make three large olive-sized cauterizations, and let them be as deep as the marrow; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of the pain in the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the hip joint, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient has been treated by what we have said in the section, and the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of the thick humors with fetid pills or other suitable pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	Afterwards, apply cauterization; and there are two types of cauterization: namely, with burning medicines and fire cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	The fire cauterization can be done in many ways, one of which is as follows: cauterize three triangular cauterizations on the hip joint in this shape, and make them deep and large, with the space between each cauterization about the thickness of a finger, and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped; sometimes a cauterization is made in the middle on the top of the hip, resulting in four cauterizations in this shape.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cauterization we mentioned previously for the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circle contains the whole hip, and that all the depth to the marrow is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the method used in sciatica, when the pain is held in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it reaches to the thigh and leg, make two cauterizations where the patient says the pain is located, and one cauterization above the ankle by four fingers’ width, slightly to the left; and let the cauterization be knife-shaped, and let it burn the thickness to the marrow; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near there, cauterize where the pain is felt with three or four points with the cauterization that is called "points."
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, make even more; and if it happens that the pain is below the knee toward the thigh, make a knife-shaped or circular cauterization, and take great care in all your cauterizations not to leave the cauterization tool on so long that you burn the nerves and the large arteries, and do not cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen several people who applied cauterization on the ankle of the foot and left it so long that the leg became completely swollen, as well as the foot, and the entire foot was pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	Afterward, there was a looseness of the stomach from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two places together, cauterize both of them in this way.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise say in the cauterization of the hip, of which here is the method, make an iron tool that is at the top as thick as a date stone, or a little less, and is grooved, and the distance from one groove to the other is about the size of a thumb joint; let the grooves be open on both sides, and shaped like knots, with a well-made iron handle; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is completely red and sparks, and then place it on the hip joint of the patient, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with a circular cauterization and leave it for three days; then apply a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after that, treat with ointments until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we rarely use this cauterization due to fear of its appearance, and we see few who use it; nevertheless, it is one of the good cauterizations, for those who can endure it, and where it is appropriate.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauterization with burning medicine is when you make an instrument with grooves where the edges of the opening descend, made of brass or iron in one long strip, and in the height there are two nodes, and between each node is the thickness of a finger; and let them be open on the outside and on top, and joined together in this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Then place it on the hip joint of the patient lying on their healthy side, and press your hand down firmly on the hip joint; then pour hot water heated a little by fire between the two circles, and leave it there for an hour, and let the patient endure its heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For they find the biting pain as if from fire; and when the burning has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and wash the hip with fresh water, and leave it this way for three days, and apply butter until what is black from the burn is removed; and leave it for three days so that the decay is extracted; and this would be the final aid before the treatment with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread to the thigh or leg, make an instrument to hold water as you did on the hip as well; and this is the hot water method, and I have written about it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and quicklime, an equal amount of each, and grind them together, and place them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small hole on the outside so that the point of a razor can enter; and put over that pot another well-sealed pot, and put alkali and lime and fresh water on top, so that there is a finger’s width above the powders when you hold it in your hand; and leave it there until water descends and falls into the sealed pot, then take all that water and pour it over lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very sharp and is administered in many medical operations and in the cauterization of other members, for it works as fire does, and there are also other medicines with which the hip is well cauterized, such as terebinth and anacardium honey and lime with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of hip pain and sciatic vein pain, and he highly praises it, saying that no other treatment was done, and that he was healed at once when this cure was done, and he bathed as he instructs hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in this way: take fresh, dry green litharge, and grind it well with a little fat, and put it on the hip and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain is, and bind it; and leave it for three hours and in such quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then put him in the bath until his body is somewhat moistened, and then put him in bed, and all the pain will leave, and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cauterization with such medicines unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat dung, it helps greatly; and the cauterization must be done in this way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and soak it in old oil, and place it on the hollow that is between the big toe and the next one, which is called the "fossette."
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Then take dry goat dung, burn it until it turns to charcoal, and place it on the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished; and repeat this process without stopping until you believe, with good sense, that the effect has reached the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this method of cauterization is called the "goat cautery."
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from a fall or a blow or from too great an evacuation, or from a spread of cold matter, none of these require cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary, after the patient has been purged with fetid pills or similar, to make three lines marked with ink on his back where the pain is, and on each line, five cauterizations or more according to the strength and amount the patient can bear; and let the cauterization be done according to the cauterization called "points"; and if you wish, make three or four cauterizations with the middle key cautery in this way:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Often, this illness comes to young children, and the signs of the beginning are that they have shortness of breath when they stand, and fear; and you will find on the last vertebra of the spine a prominence that stands out over the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you wish to cure it, then cauterize it with the circular cautery in this way.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery reaches each part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the pricking cautery, in two or three lines, with the points close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Then treat the area until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to administer cauterization on a hump caused by nerve spasm.
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain of the joints is from moistures that are spread to each member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which physicians call "gout" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, it is cured by cauteries in this way: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-like in this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary for you to cauterize on the face of the foot, make the cautery with the cautery they call "point."
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come down to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, make a cautery on each knee, three or four cauteries on each part, with the olive-like cautery; and if you need more, make more, but do not hold your hand there longer than until the thickness of the flesh is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the wrist in two lines; and if any pain remains in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the top of the hand; and if the pains come down to the elbows or up to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and give good care to the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give good care to him and purge the phlegm, he will be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the scrotum
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes with swelling, and the intestines descend into the testicles, and it is recent, it is necessary that, when you want to treat it, he should not eat that day; and that he uses things that loosen the stomach, so that the waste descends from his belly; then make him sit on his back between your hands, and tell him to hold his breath until the intestines are returned, and move them back with your fingers, and cauterize below the rupture on the bone of the wrist, with a mark resembling a half-circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and throws sparks.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then return the intestines to their place; and the assistant should hold his hand there so they do not come back; and work well with the patient’s thighs, and put a cushion under him and a helper on the thighs, and another on the chest who holds his hands; then put the cautery on the mark with your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it there until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, repeat it again until you come to the bone; and watch carefully that the intestines do not protrude when you apply the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that because of this the patient does not die, or suffer other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to the measure of their bones, and for adults as large according to their measure; after three days, treat the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is gone; afterward treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie forty days on his back until the wound is well fused; and it is necessary that his nourishment be sustained for a long time, so that the intestines do not protrude when he begins to walk in rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, administer a well-made bandage to him, and he should wear it forty more days; and let him have good rest, work little, and guard against too great a filling of food and drink, and from shouting too loudly; and when he follows this guidance he is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will speak hereafter of the cure of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other areas of the abdomen and are apparent, and you wish that they do not grow further, make a rounded cautery according to its size, and let a third of the flesh be burned; afterward, treat it according to what we have said; and some of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized with a three-angled cautery in this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the hip and make a line along the width above the rupture, and another above, and place your hand in the middle with the pointed cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of chronic pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any member, from falling or striking, and this pain lasts a long time, and the cures of medicine are of no value, then it is necessary to cauterize it with a cautery called "point," and the cautery should be according to the length of the member and its smallness and its weakness and strength and the location of the twists and of its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, begin another cautery on that one, for such a practice is that it should move to the member nearest to it, for which reason you must make the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of leprosy
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The leprous are sometimes aided by cautery to a great extent, and especially those illnesses that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you wish to cauterize it, observe if the illness is at its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and it does not descend or remain, and you fear that corruption may overtake the whole patient, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head at the top, and the other toward the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two sides, and one behind on the crown; and hold your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the heavy humors can come out; and cauterize on the same area as it was before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	And if the leprosy is spread everywhere, and it appears visibly, then you must cauterize it with these cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery on the top of the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the sacrum and another beside it, and two on the two shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the chest, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and take care with the nerves that are near the sacrum, that you do not burn them; and sometimes one makes a cautery on the wrist bone, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more cauteries you make, the more you help him, and the more he benefits; and know that the patient does not feel the pain of the cautery as a healthy person would, because the body is already all corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And the cauteries must be large and small according to the members and the joints, according to what you will find in types of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterward, treat the place with bean flour with honey and other cures until he is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling appears in a limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, and it is not healed, then a cautery is applied to the limb according to the size and shape of the limb; and the cautery should penetrate slightly into the thickness of the flesh; then it is treated with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes a cautery is applied to the hand, the foot, and the back, at the exit point of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; however, no one should undertake this unless they know the limbs and the paths of the nerves that move the body.
de albaras	Regarding albaras
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" becomes chronic and the medicines no longer work, then it is cauterized with a slightly deep cautery, according to the thickness of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and the color is changed; then it is treated with a paste of vetch flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and the blood of pigeon and swallow, one part of each; all should be mixed together, wrapped in a cloth, and left in place until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of chancre by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When chancre appears in the beginning and you wish to stop it, it is cauterized with a circular cautery, all around the edge of the chancre.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	However, the wise ones say that a cautery should also be made in the center of the chancre; nonetheless, this does not seem good to me, for I fear it may ulcerate and become corrupt, as I have already seen happen at times; it is better that it be cauterized all around with the cautery called "circle," as we have described in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Regarding the swelling that cannot mature
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it delays maturing, whether due to the excess it creates or due to the age of the patient when they are decrepit (meaning very old) and they have little blood, or due to the time; and you wish to hasten its maturation: then it is cauterized around with many small piercing cauteries; afterwards, leave it as it is.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to mature.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you wish to pierce it entirely with the cautery, then heat the cautery of this shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the center of the disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the flesh, and the cautery should be such that the patient feels it externally in such a way that the course of the rot is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, treat it until it is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The treatment of fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another type of disease called "corrodens," which is nothing other than an eating away of the limb, for it consumes the limbs as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can withstand both cautery and fire, then heat the cautery tools, both small and large, according to what is needed for the area where the disease is; then cauterize all around until you remove all the corruption, and nothing of it remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then leave it for three days, and apply powdered sulfur mixed with oil on the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are removed, along with all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	Afterwards, treat it with ointments that promote flesh growth.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days you see that healthy flesh does not begin to grow, that is good; if not, then redo the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this eating away has sometimes been cured with strong medicine instead of fire cautery; however, fire cautery is more effective, and I have already given the cure with strong medicine in the division: use it when you have need of it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of calluses that appear on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times, a disease appears on the feet from the outside, which we call "clos," and it is a hard growth that harms the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization for this disease is of two kinds.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	These are fire cautery and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat a cautery tip shaped like a bird’s feather, made of good iron to fit around the callus on all sides, with fine edges; then place it, very hot, on the callus, and move your hand all around the callus until it reaches the base of the callus; then leave it for three days until it starts expelling decay; then make a poultice of crushed wild mallow with salt, and leave the poultice on overnight, and the callus will fall away and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the area with an ointment that promotes flesh growth until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are present on the outer part of the body, and this often happens on both hands and feet, then you need to administer hot water cautery in this way: take a small tube of copper or iron, or a bird’s feather, and place it over the callus or wart; set the tube so that it surrounds the entire area, then pour a little hot water into it, hold your hand steady, and press down while turning so that the tube’s edge reaches the root of the callus, allowing the hot water to penetrate deeply to the root; the patient should endure the bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it, and it will uproot itself completely along with its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this one after another until you have uprooted all those on the body, then treat them with ointments that generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles from nerve coldness, quartan fever, or another cause, you should make four cauterizations on the spine of the back, one between each vertebra; and one cauterization on the foot, and one on the stomach with the olive-shaped cautery; this will stop the trembling, and health will be hastened for the cold illness.
des pustules puans	Of foul-smelling pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes, swellings or foul-smelling pustules appear on the surface of the body, which come from decayed humors.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	As soon as they appear, you should cauterize the top of each pustule: a delicate cautery made of myrtle wood, with its tip heated in fire, or from the root of long aristolochia, or with a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this way, and they cannot grow any further, as the excess that caused them is interrupted, and they are healed; but it must be done after bloodletting.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times, there is heavy bleeding from an artery that is cut by an external wound, by the incision of an abscess, by the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is very difficult to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very firmly until the blood calms under your finger, and no drop escapes; then put several small and large olive-shaped cautery tools in the fire until they are all red-hot; then take one, either large or small depending on the wound and the place where the artery is broken, and put the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery has cooled, quickly take another of the cauteries from the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	Do not stop doing this one after the other until the blood is stanched; and be careful not to burn the nearby nerve, and so that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be easily stanched, especially when the artery is large, except by one of the four methods we have mentioned: by cautery, by pulling out when it is not torn, by strong binding with thread, or by medicines applied on it that have the power to stanch blood; and it should be tied and bound properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Applying tight bandages of cloth, or placing burning things on it, or similar measures, will be of little help in stanching the flow.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if it happens to someone who has no doctor or medicine available, he should place his index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press firmly until it is stanched on the wound and on the vein; and do not move the finger, but wet it often with very cold water until the blood is congealed, thickened, and stanched; and thereafter do what is needed in terms of cautery and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of cures by incision
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter of every illness in which a cautery of fire or burning medicine is necessary, and the requirements, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have set out that chapter from head to foot, and I will proceed in this chapter in the same way so that what one seeks may be found more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And before I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first concerning cauteries, and for this, greater caution is needed.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there often occurs bloodletting in opening the vein, and incision on abscesses, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in the incision over stones, and similar things; where there is fear and doubt, and many come to death from it.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Some come who are so afflicted with their illness that they die easily because of the madness caused by their illness, and the magnitude of their suffering; and one must be wary of these.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And among these, there are those who give you their judgment and say, “Wait, I am healed”; and the illness is merciless.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not fitting that you yield to those who come to you in such a manner; instead, place more trust in your honor than in your desire for gain, and do not operate foolishly but wisely in that which you are certain of, and from which you can gain reward and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients, so that healing may be achieved; and this will help you acquire a good reputation, glory, and a memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dearest son, may Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and may He inspire you with the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have arranged this chapter, dividing it by chapters, in the same way as the previous chapter on cauteries, which I have set out from head to foot, so that you may more easily find what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Of a head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife squeezes the child’s head too hard; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness except in children, and in all those I have seen, death came quickly; and for this reason, it seems to me best to abandon treatment in such cases.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and the head swelled each day so much that he could not hold it up; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture collects under the bone above the dura mater, between the brain and the bone; and the procedure is as follows: if the moisture is between the brain and the bone, and the swelling is small, you make a large incision in the middle of the head; and it should be as long as two fingers, enough for the moisture to flow; and here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is greater and the swelling larger, then make two incisions in the shape of a cross, in this manner:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the seams of the head opened on each side, and the water spurts out when you press it inward with your hand, and it has not been held back: then you must make three incisions in the middle of the head, in this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, draw out all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Then bind the incisions with cloths and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then uncover it, and treat the wound with dressings and ointments, and keep the head wrapped evenly, and give the patient dry food with little moisture so that the body is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is to observe where the swelling of the abscess and the accumulation of water are visible; for sometimes it is in the front, sometimes in the back, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Make the incision where the swelling and the water accumulation are apparent, and cut according to your skill; and take care not to cut the artery; and let the blood flow so that the patient does not die from bleeding and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	Of rheum
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone suffers from an illness called "catarrh" of the eyes or chest, and the illness is chronic, and medical treatments have not helped, then the final treatment is cautery along with cutting the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then, when you intend to cut them, the patient must tilt back his head; then rub the area with a rough cloth until the arteries are visible, then the patient should tie his neck with a cloth; then observe where the vein pulses, and the places of each are behind the ears, and they are barely held back; then mark the places with ink, then cut each with a sharp spatula on both sides, until the cut reaches the bone, and this should be across the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you wish, place the spatula beneath the artery and cut above it, cutting across about two finger-widths.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut, the blood spurts out continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery is not easily felt, measure about three finger-widths, then mark with ink and cut down to the bone; and the required amount of blood to be released is six ounces, perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can endure and the artery's fullness; then examine the wound: if anything remains on the bone near the dura mater, cut it away so that no hot abscess appears there, then compress and bind the wound, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When chronic migraine comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moisture from tears and heat in the temples, and old stubborn pain and similar conditions, and it is treated with various medicinal remedies and none of that helps, then we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extracting them is that the patient shaves the hair of his temples and locates the artery that is visible in the temple, as it shows well by its pulse, and it is barely held back except in some men who are very cold; and if it is held back, the patient should bind his neck with a cloth, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and sprinkle the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula shaped as follows:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then lightly scrape the skin until you reach the artery, then draw it up with pincers, and carefully separate it from the tissues that are beneath it on each side; and if the artery is thin, turn it around the tip of the hook, then cut it at that point about two heads’ width.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, the blood will not spurt out entirely.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out six ounces of blood, up to three; and if the artery is large, it must be tied in two places with a strong double silk thread, to prevent infection from forming before the wound is sealed, and to prevent the flow of blood; then cut the excess between the two ligatures at that moment, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with a knife cautery down to the bone so that the tips are cut; and this is the best approach, if the patient has no fever and is of warm temperament.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery helps to end the moisture: for this reason, it is of great help for moist conditions.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where necessary for the extraction of arteries, fill the area with old cotton and place properly prepared tents on it; and when they are loosened, treat them with dry medicines that generate flesh, and with tents, until it is healed; and if blood flows from the artery while you are working, then hasten to stop it with cautery, or fill the area with vitriol and press it with your hand until the blood is stopped; and if you do not have this at hand, place your finger over the area until the blood coagulates, and sprinkle the area with cold water until the bleeding stops, and bind it as needed; and the best and easiest way for extracting the artery is to cauterize the vein with a double-edged cautery, but the edges should be quite thick to retain their heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it retains its heat less.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be one finger’s width of space between the two blades, and when you have marked the two places with ink, you place the heated iron on it until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and the two ends should be separated, because it is not completely sealed with this cautery; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes descend from the veins on the exterior of the head, and no treatment with medicine is beneficial, you see the face of the patient redden, and he feels a trembling in the forehead; and his eyes are cloudy and moist so that the hairs of the eyelids have fallen, and the eyelids are inflamed and chafed from the heat of the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And the ancients called this “bruised cure,” and it consists of shaving the patient’s forehead, who has this affliction, then making three incisions in the forehead evenly along its length; one incision should be about two fingers wide, right in the middle of the forehead going down to the nose, and the other two on either side above the eyelids, taking care to avoid cutting the arteries located on both sides above the eyelids; keep your hand away from the joint of the two jawbones, and each wound should be about three fingers wide across; have ready a piece of sponge and plenty of cloth to wipe the blood, then apply the sharp spatula in two parts, shaped as follows:
