A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many men develop a hard swelling inside the lips, resembling grains of vetch, both smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips and cut over each nodule, grab it with forceps and cut it into each part; then fill the spot after the incision with powdered vitriol, until the blood is stanched; then wash it with vinegar, and treat the spot with drying substances until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh on the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Sometimes additional flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; then you must hold it with forceps, cut it at the root, and let the pus or blood flow; then apply powdered vitriol, or other constricting and drying powders, to the spot; and if this flesh grows back after the incision, as often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it: it will not return after cauterization; and these are the types of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of the tartar
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, on the tips of the teeth inside the mouth between the gums, crusts form that are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, to the point that the corruption reaches the gums, and the teeth are foul-smelling; then you must make the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your chest, and scrape the teeth where the crusts appear, until nothing remains; and do the same with the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are clean; and if you can remove everything on the first pass, it is good; if not, begin again on the second and third days until you have scraped everything; and know that the teeth need different types of instruments for scraping, according to what the work shows, because the scrapers used to scrape the front of the teeth have different forms from those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a toothache, you must delay extraction as long as you can, for it should not be done; it is a most valued substance, to the point where there is no excuse for scraping.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	So when the patient is forced to extraction, you must be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors. et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles. et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain torments the patient, and he thinks it is in the healthy tooth, causing him to have the good tooth pulled; yet the pain does not stop from that, because the bad one remains, as we have seen happen to these lords. And when you are certain of the aching tooth, you must scrape around the tooth with a strong spatumile to protect the gum on all sides; then move it with your fingers or fine forceps bit by bit, until it is well loosened, then firmly secure the forceps on it. And place the patient’s head in your lap between your knees, holding it well so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	Then extract the tooth straight out without breaking it, and if it does not come loose, take one of these instruments and insert it lightly on each side, and loosen it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten away, you must fill it with small pieces of cloth where the holes are; then press it carefully with the forceps, so it does not break from the pressure; and you must work very gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And take great care not to break it, leaving a part behind, as worse pain than before may return to the patient from the remaining root.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut. et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware not to do as ignorant practitioners do, who sometimes, out of haste and boldness, break the chariot and do not manage it as we have advised; for they sometimes cause great illness due to the roots that remain or the broken chariot, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, as often happens, fill the spot with powdered vitriol; and if this is not enough, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the instruments, with which one first moves the teeth, should have long points and thick handles, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick so that they do not bend when pulling, be made of good-quality steel, and have teeth to grip well.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after pulling, you should place moistened cotton with butter on the spot for one or two days,
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened, then place the pincers called "algefri," whose head resembles a hawk's beak; and let them be fashioned on the inside like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with these pincers, you should uncover the flesh around the root and place the instrument called "althali," which is a type of lever, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so it does not break, and if the root dislodges from it, that is good; if not, make use of all the instruments, whose forms are shown hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And so one uses this instrument that has two branches, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and of other iron tools which are for the teeth, and this instrument that resembles large pincers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s  et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be strong so it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for teeth; also, other instruments that are not mentioned; and the wise, skilled master finds for himself his own instrument, according to what his work and the illness show him, for there are certain illnesses for which the ancients did not teach any instrument because of the variety of cases; and if one breaks any part of the cartilage or other bones, or if it rots, search among the instruments that are appropriate, as I have told you, and use the forceps, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and strong to hold the bone so it does not slip, but can be held and removed; then restore the area with appropriate medicines, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, remove it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie;  et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not in the natural alignment, and the shape is unpleasant, especially in young women, you should find out if the tooth is born after the other teeth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be filed or smoothed: then extract it; and if it is attached to the tooth, then take this instrument, whose form is here, resembling a small beak, and let it be of hardened iron with a sharp tip:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And cut it little by little over several days due to the hardness of the tooth, and so as not to disturb the others, and if it is possible to file it, then file it with this type of file, whose form is here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the files used to make needles; and file the tooth little by little over several days, gently, so that it does not loosen so much that it falls out; then smooth it at the end with some type of scraper, and if the tooth is too sharp and it wounds the tongue, it should be filed until it is even, so that it does not injure the tongue or impair speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth become loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth become loose, either from an impact or from falling, and the patient cannot press on what he eats without them falling out, and if you have treated them with astringent medicines and this does not work, then they must be restrained with a gold thread, because silver thread turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and the thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you want to straighten the teeth, then take the thread and push it doubled between the two healthy teeth, then place the ends between the loose teeth, if there is one or several, until you wisely reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering up to the place where you started, and delicately and wisely tighten your hand, so that it does not move at all; and your tying should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the ends of the thread with pincers, and join them together, and place them between the healthy tooth, and set it so it does not wound the tongue; and then leave it thus tight as long as it can hold, and if it loosens or the thread breaks, then tighten it with another thread; it will remain and serve in this way for its entire time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the form of aligning the two healthy teeth and the two loose ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, one puts it back in its place, freshly, as we have said; and let no one attempt this who is not wise and patient, and sometimes one makes the form of a tooth from cow bone, and places it where there is a gap, and binds it as we have said, and it stays and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	On cutting the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament is located under the tongue from birth, as one is born this way; or by accident from a healed wound; and the procedure is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head to your breast, and lift his tongue; then cut the nerve ligament broadly, until the tongue is freed from its attachment, and if there is hardness or a knot, and it is from wound healing, then insert the hook and cut that ligament broadly; and make sure the cut is not too deep, because of the artery below; and when you have finished, then wash the area with rose water and plantain water, or with cold water, then place a linen tent under the tongue; and the patient should hold it there every night, so the area cannot reattach.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is blood flow, then place powdered vitriol on the spot; and if the blood overwhelms you, then cauterize it with the blunt cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is discolored or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a cancer; and if it is tending toward whiteness, and there is moisture, then insert the hook, and make a fine cut with a delicate scalpel, and loosen it from one side and the other; and if blood overwhelms you in your work, then place powdered vitriol on it until it is stilled, then return to your work until you extract all the infection; then wash the area with plantain and salt water, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	On abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes swellings appear inside the throat which are called "godath," and they are properly called the two tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the section, and they are not healed, then pay attention: if it is a hard abscess of little volume and of a dark color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, also do not touch it with iron, for the risk of bleeding; but let it ripen, and then you will open it, or it will burst on its own; and if it is pale in color and rounded, and the root is delicate, then have your instrument ready to cut, but first make sure that the hot abscess has settled and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then seat the patient facing the sun, with his head at your breast, and open his mouth, and the assistant holds him with his hands, and presses down the tongue with the instrument, of which here is the shape; and it should be made of silver or fine brass like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with this instrument, and you see the abscess, then take the hook and insert it into the tonsil, and pull it out above as much as you can; and bring with it some of the tissues, then cut it with the instrument, the shape of which is here, resembling pincers; and both heads are curved, one toward the other, and are very sharp, and it is made of Indian iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, then cut it with pincers, of which here is the shape:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side, and not on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, the patient should gargle with warm water, and plantain water, and if there is bleeding, the patient should gargle with water, or with boiled pomegranate peels, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is staunched; then treat it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat besides the two tonsils, so cut them then as you did the two tonsils alike.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had grown inside her throat, that is to say, a small abscess; and it had almost entirely closed off her throat, so that the woman could not breathe because the passage was blocked, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she remained so for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had already grown so much that it had pushed two roots out through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hurried immediately, and inserted a hook into one nostril, then pulled it out, and extracted a large portion of pus; then I repeated the same in the other nostril, opened her mouth and pressed down her tongue; then I inserted the hook into the abscess, and cut away part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the woman’s throat passage was cleared, and she immediately began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop trimming this abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing back, filling up the area I had cleared, until it became very large again; then I burned it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I departed from those parts, and I do not know what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	On the uvula
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When phlegm descends to the uvula, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendiculaire"; and if it is round and thick below, it is called "uve."
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the section, and the treatment is of no use, and you see that the hot abscess is settled and it is delicate, it is necessary for you to cut it; and the one that is round and not elongated; and if it is red, dark, or black in color, you must avoid cutting it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to what I have said, of its whiteness and length, make the patient sit facing the sun, and press down his tongue with the instrument which we mentioned above; then insert the hook into the uvula, pull it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments I mentioned in the incision of the two tonsils.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And be sure to cut only the excess that extends beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it will harm the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two tonsils, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient is afraid of the cutting, then you should use a cauterizing technique without fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of cauterizing is very sharp.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	The patient should rest his head against your chest, then press down his tongue with the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cauterizing, and mix it with warm distilled water, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and fill the end of this instrument with it, of which here is the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And at the top there is a tuft of hair where the medicine is placed, about the size of a spoonful, and place the instrument with the medicine on the uvula; and the patient should lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth from the medicine inside, so that it does not go down the throat and harm it; then hold your hand with the medicine and press it on the uvula for about half an hour, until you see it blacken and the stinging of the medicine is soothed; and if you want, take cotton and wrap it on an instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and push the instrument with the cotton into the throat above, so that the cotton sticks to the uvula; and do this often, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and it falls off after four or five days; and if you need to repeat the cauterization with the medicine, then repeat it, and after the cauterization, wipe around the uvula with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and it should be rinsed with cold water, and treated with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is treated by fumigation according to this method, take calamint, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, oats, and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in a pot, and add garlic, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument with a head according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or brass, and one end of it should be placed in the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the uvula through the throat, until the uvula is numbed; then repeat it often, until the uvula dries, and make sure not to do this at the beginning of the onset of the hot abscess, because many things can occur; and do it only at the decline of the hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, then take a tube and put inside it the end of an eggshell, so that the mouth of the patient does not get too hot; for the eggshell prevents the vapor from irritating the mouth, and this is a good treatment along with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often a bone or fish spine or something else becomes stuck in the throat; it is then necessary to pull out what you can see, and press the tongue into the light with an instrument, so that you can see where the object is lodged; and for what is not visible and is stuck in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; by chance the object will come out by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will catch, and then you will pull it out; and if it does not come out from what we have said, then take an instrument of lead shaped in this way:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can more easily enter the throat, and have the end raised upward; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest it cause a cough, nor push the bone further in; and it is best if the patient inserts the instrument there himself, so that he can feel where the object is lodged; then either push it downward, or pull it out with the instrument evenly, until it is removed.
de la sansue de la gorge	About the leech in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the leech is treated, as I have said in the section, with medicinal treatment; and when this does not help, then look into the patient’s throat in the sunlight, while you press down the tongue with the instrument that I mentioned to you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, pull it out with a small hook, or with fine tongs suited for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, then take a hollow tube, and insert it into the patient's throat, then put a hot iron at the end of the tube, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And let the patient hold water in their mouth all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a glass full of cold water, open the mouth, and pour it in without swallowing, and the patient moves it around in their mouth often; and as soon as the leech feels the water, it will fall off.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall off as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the instrument that I mentioned for fumigating the uvula; do this many times, for it will fall off without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot in which there are live coals, and the pot is covered with a lid pierced in the middle, and in this hole the head of the instrument is placed; then you throw your fumigation in, and the sick person places the end of the tube in their mouth and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape but reaches the leech; and the leech will soon fall off, and if it does not, repeat the fumigation several times; and the sick person should endure thirst and eat salty and other foods, and not drink any water; and then it will be necessary that it [the leech] come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which the leech is pulled out is, when one can see it, like curved pincers for reaching deep into the throat; it resembles a bird’s beak, and has the roughness of a file, so that what it grabs it cannot release; and here is the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, as is remembered further on in this book, and they vary in perforation and size; there are two types, one of which is in its own nature, and it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second type is according to the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For an abscess on the head is different from one at the base, and an abscess on a fleshy area is different from one that forms in joints, and each has its particular treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the swelling has matured; and there are others that must be pierced when they have grown, and do not mature fully, like abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess appears near joints and is left until it has rotted around, then the ligaments and nerves of the joint may become damaged, which may cause contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is near a principal organ, and if you delay the piercing until it has matured, it will damage the principal organ; or if it is near the base, it should be pierced before it matures; and you should not pierce a swollen abscess without complete digestion, except for one near the base, lest it rot deeply, extend inward, and form a fistula, which cannot heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time to pierce an abscess that has matured, which is when the pain has subsided, and the fever has reduced, and the lessening of the pain and the redness, and the throbbing and the sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and you must make the perforation in the most dependent part of the abscess, where it appears most swollen; and the perforation should be along the length of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints, or near nerves or arteries, or in areas where there is no bend.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those that bend, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy area, it is often better to delay the piercing until it is fully digested, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body will be filled with the poison of it, and full of much filth; and the edges and depth of it may harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And there are some abscesses that are pierced across the width of the body, according to what the limb requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must administer small punctures in small abscesses, and large punctures in large abscesses, with many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and there are some abscesses where you must remove the core, and cut; when it has already become like a dead flap, it is necessary to treat it as one does with boils: and there are some that are cut in three corners, and some where it is cut like a myrtle leaf, as with groin abscesses; and there are some where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar incisions.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those that have no head, such as a soft, superficial abscess, must be fully pierced; and when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not drain all the pus at once, but remove part of it; then plug the abscess until the next day, and then draw out some again; do this many times gradually until all the pus comes out; especially if the patient is of weak strength, or a pregnant woman, or a young child, or an old man weakened by age.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirit sometimes leaps out with the release of the pus, and perhaps the patient may die, and you would not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, proceed through this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, wipe the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; if it is a shallow cut, apply plugs of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess with many holes, it is necessary to insert a plug into each one so that they press against each other; and if you have cut into the abscess part of the skin and turned it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your operation, apply cold water and vinegar, soak a cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, provide care and treatment, and use the powders I have mentioned in several places in this book, and if it is in winter, and the area where the abscess is located is very sensitive, then you must apply plugs and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is in summer, and the area is fleshy, then you must apply cloths soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil, until the third day, as we have said; then uncover the abscess, wipe it and treat it as necessary until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	Of cysts
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	In the center of the head come small abscesses, similar to knots in fabrics, like the yolk of an egg, and many resemble this.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	Some are fatty, and others contain moisture like pus; there are also some that are hard and stony to cut, without any doubt unless the artery interferes.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the operation of cutting is such that you test it with an instrument called an "entromissoire," whose form is described below, to determine what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then cut it open lengthwise.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, peel away all of the skin that contained this moisture, for it will soon return if anything is left; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and salt, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day; this will drain what remains overnight.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then reapply the cotton as before, on the second day and the third, until you are sure that nothing remains overnight; then treat the wound with the appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds a fatty kernel, cut it in this way, lengthwise; apply your ointments, peel it from all sides, and focus all your care on removing the membrane in which it lies; and if the artery gives you trouble, do as I told you earlier.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do likewise if the abscess is stony, following the instructions I gave for cutting and treating.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cutting a stony or moist abscess is easier, as they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And some of these abscesses in the head contain no moisture, as was the case with an abscess I cut from the head of an old woman; I found the abscess like a deaf stone, rough and white, which could not be broken; if anyone had struck it, they would have caused a wound as if from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that appear in the head, except for those that occur on children's heads and at the roots of the ears, the opening should always be at the lowest point, to allow the pus to drain; and treat them as necessary.
des scrophules	Of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often, these abscesses appear on the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they appear elsewhere on the body, and they are numerous and are joined together.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own shell, like the knots and abscesses of the head, as we have said; and the forms of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not respond to healing.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	For one that you see has a good disposition to the touch, resembles the color of the body, and moves freely on all sides and is not connected to the nerves of the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep; you must cut it from above, peeling it from each side, and stretch the two lips of the core with forceps, if you need them, as we mentioned in abscesses of the head; draw it out bit by bit, and be sure not to cut the nerve or the vein, and do not let the spatula be sharp or cutting, so the hand does not slip, nor go too deep, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and this does not allow you to proceed, then put powdered vitriol in the wound, or some powders that stop bleeding, and compress the wound; and leave it until the swelling is reduced, and the wound is softened, and begins to decay.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you finish it; then check with your index finger if any small lumps remain, and cut and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the lump, you must not cut that lump at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut the entire lump, you must bring the two edges of the wound together, and sew them immediately, since there is no excess remaining due to the size of the lump.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	You must then focus on cutting its root, and drawing out the pus, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those lumps that contain excess, pierce them where it appears ripe; and pierce it like the one previously mentioned, hanging downward, then administer tents with ointment and similar substances, so that it corrupts what remains of the infection; and when the wound is well cleaned, treat it with ointment that generates flesh, until it is healed.
de squinance	of quinsy
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and wrote of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and it is only the writings of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have quinsy, the cut in the throat called the “epiglottis” must be avoided; and assistance should not be given in this way, because all the veins and lungs of the patient are affected in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat or in both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the canal of the lung, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Then, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we must make a small horizontal cut below the third or fourth ring, between the two rings or by the width of the opening of the trachea, but not in the cartilage; and this place is suitable for the cutting of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are distant from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat with a hook, then cut down to the trachea; avoid the blood vessels if you see anything, and then cut the trachea, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the flow of phlegm from the trachea that escapes from the open place, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time of danger of strangulation has passed, bring together the two edges of the wound in the throat, and sew it together carefully, sparing the cartilage; then apply medicines that generate flesh, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that this should not be done unless the throat is completely blocked, the patient is considered near death, and breath fails.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and so the ancients advised leaving the wound open until the malignancy of the disease has passed, which takes three or four days. Then they advised sewing and treating the wound, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young woman who took a knife, and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the lung channels; and I was called to treat her, and found her almost dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had flowed from it, and I knew well that she had not cut any vein or duct other than the throat, and air was escaping through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sewed the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and nothing happened to the young woman except that her voice was hoarse, and later returned to normal; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the swollen throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This swelling is called a “hernia of the throat,” and is a large swelling, yellow in color, and is very common in women; and it occurs in two forms: natural and accidental; the natural form has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental form has two varieties, one resembling a fatty lump, and the other resembling a swelling that comes from an artery; and be cautious with it, and only operate with instruments on the smaller one, and test and search it thoroughly with the probe: if you find it like a fatty lump, and it does not attach to any vein, then cut it as one cuts lumps, and remove it with its sheath, if it has one; then carefully inspect everything, and treat it as needed, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	Of swellings
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many types of swellings, of which I will speak all varieties; and now I need to explain the difference between swelling and abscess.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess includes heat and fever until the swelling has subsided, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and the heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a swelling there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains a sac which is its own, colored like the body, and starts small like a pea, then grows larger; they take two forms, either firm or moist, and in many colors, as I said in the description.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you proceed to treat a swelling, you must test and examine it first with the instrument called a "probe," according to its form, which will be described in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to examine an abscess in a swelling is to take the softest place you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers bit by bit, until you are sure the instrument has reached the core, according to the size of the abscess; then withdraw the probe and observe what flows out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If fluid runs out, note what color it is and treat it as I have instructed with other abscesses; if no moisture flows from the probe, know it is firm, so cut it crosswise, grasp it with the pincers, and gently strip away the skin from each side, making sure to draw it out whole with the swelling; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then take it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains, the swelling will return many times; and if a little remains and blood troubles you, fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powder, press the wound, and apply soothing substances, and treat the abscess with other remedies until it is healed; and if the swelling is large, sew the two edges of the wound, and treat it to help new flesh grow.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if a pulsating vein is in your way or otherwise, hurry and fill the place with crushed vitriol, and leave it tied for two or three days until the wound putrefies, allowing the blood to settle; then return to cut whatever remains of the swelling.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the types of probes, and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small; there are also three square ones called “albaret,” and one called “breb,” and these also come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, for exploring fistulous abscesses; they are like the needles used for sewing stitches, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are the best, and the black lead ones are more effective for exploring the curvatures of fistulae; they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, depending on the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of hooks are of many types, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are hooks with two curves in three types as well; there are hooks with three curves, and these also come in three types; there are hooks with two curves, and hooks with only one curve, and all come in three types; and all of these are necessary in their respective places.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The ends of these with which one cuts are sharp, and among them are some that only cut on one side, with which one scrapes flesh, so as not to sever the vein or the nerve; and of these instruments, some blades are fitted into handles so that the patient does not notice during the opening of abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are used only in fleshy areas, such as the legs, arms, breasts, groin, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument resembling pistachio shells, according to this form, with which one staunches blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes placed on the area that bleeds from the cutting of veins and arteries, and sometimes it is reused according to this large form.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to become diseased, so that they resemble the breasts of a woman; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wishes to treat them must cauterize according to this form from line .b. to line .g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then strip away the fat, and fill the wound with a medicine that generates flesh, then bring together the two lips of the wound with stitches, and care for it until it is healed; and if the breast droops downward and is softened by its size, as happens in women, then cut it in two places above, with two similar incisions; one should connect to the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller one in this form, from line .b. to line .g.; then strip the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said of stitches and powders, and what is necessary in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not fully made, because the patient does not wish to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with cotton moistened in a corrosive ointment; and leave it until it eats away the remainder and the fat, then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that appear beneath the armpits are types of hard scrofula that have roots, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess is drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, then cut it as we have described for scrofulous incisions, and if the wound oozes pus, apply the cautery as we have previously described.
de la routure de l’artere	On the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is broken, and the skin above it is attached, abscesses often form, and the same happens with the swollen vein and abscess; and one recognizes it thus: when it is due to the artery, the abscess is long and deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel a tightness; and when it is due to the vein, it is round and visibly apparent; and it is foolish to cut this abscess, especially when it is below the armpits, in the groin, the neck, and in many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.
