One must therefore avoid using the iron for treatment, and likewise avoid it for the head; and in the case of a swelling of the artery, make an incision lengthwise through the skin; then open the incision with forceps, and carefully separate the artery from the tissues until it is exposed; then place a needle underneath it and pierce through to the other side, and tie the artery with a double thread in two places, as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then prick the place between the two ligatures with a probe so that the blood contained there may flow out, and let the abscess drain; then administer the treatment that produces scabs, until the threads fall off; then treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed; and if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, you must hold as much of the abscess and all the skin as you can with your hand, then place the needle under the place you hold with your hand, and pierce it through, with a double thread so that you draw it through to the other side; then tie off the abscess, as I have told you, with the tying of one of the two parts at the two ends of the thread; and if you fear that the thread will come out, then insert another needle with a thread underneath the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the threads in four places; then cut the abscess so that the excess flows out, then cut the excess from the center and leave that which is tied; then place on top a cloth moistened in wine and oil, then administer tenting and ointment treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	On abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Just as abscesses appear in the artery and vein, abscesses appear in the nerves when they are struck or from too much work, and similar causes.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens more often in the wrists, fingers, and all places with joints, and it is a severe abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and in many cases, it is without pain; and when it is pressed hard, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep in the body, but just under the skin; and it moves easily in all directions, and does not go forward or backward, nor below or above, and for the one that is in joints, it should not be cut with iron: by chance, it might cause contraction; and for one on the head or forehead, the skin should be split with a spatumile.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with pincers, and cut it at its root; and if it is large, suspend it with a hook, peel it, then remove it and close the wound with stitches, and care for it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	On large, hanging lumps
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Sometimes on the belly and nowhere else occurs a growth, which is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and its root is fine, and its head large; and some are small, and some are very large; and I saw a man who had two on his belly which looked more like mushrooms than anything else, and there was no difference in appearance, and they were white, and had thin roots, and were already split, and moisture constantly flowed from them.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them off and found one weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six ounces, and the procedure in the incision is that you see if the growth is moist, and the color of the swelling is white and moist and has a fine root; then cut it with a broad spatumile, and have the cauterizing tool in the fire in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For during cutting, there often comes too much bleeding, and if the blood overwhelms you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the incision by the iron, then take a well-made lead wire, and tie the swelling with it as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not stop tightening the lead wire until it cuts the swelling, and it falls off on its own without effort; and if the roots are large, there is reason to fear cutting it, especially for the belly, but you can safely cut half of it, then cauterize it so it does not regrow; then treat the wound, and take care not to cut the growth that is of a reddish color and of poor texture and unsightly appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an ulcerated abscess, and I will come to the treatment of ulcers hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the hernia appears outside
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the hernia arises from cautery of a wound or from rupture of the peritoneum, and is on the abdomen with some of the intestines emerging, as happens in other ruptures, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries as stated above, or from gas; and if it is due to a rupture of the peritoneum and by the exit of the bowel, the color of the abscess resembles the color of the body, and it is a minor condition without pain, and appears with various symptoms.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the exit of the intestine, then it is more unusual, and when pressed with the fingers it recedes, and then returns, and by chance it is constricted, and it enlarges greatly upon entering the bath and from heavy labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a minor condition, and it is clear when you press it with your hand, and it is not constricted; and if it is due to blood, the signs show the abscess as large and hard, and it is fixed to a certain size; and if it is due to gas, it is soft to the touch, and the procedure is to examine whether the appearance is from blood of the artery, or of the vein, or from gas.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	Then it is necessary that you refrain from treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear in this, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the bowel, you must instruct the patient to hold his breath and lie fully extended, then mark in ink all around the hernia; then instruct him to lie steadily in your hands, then go around the marked place with the spatumile, then extend the upper half of the abscess with the large hook; then tie it around firmly with a strong thread or a strong silk cord, and the knot of the tie should be secure; then open the half of the abscess stretched over the tie, and insert your index finger and locate the intestine; if you find it caught by the tie, untie it and push the intestine back into the abdomen; and if you find the bowel, take it with the hook and cut away the excess; and if the artery or the vein gives you trouble, carefully go around it, then return to your task and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and place the two needles around the area you marked in a cross where you made the incision; then tighten the abscess in four places on the needles, and if you wish, remove the needles, and leave the area until it rots, and the dead flesh falls off by itself; or cut it away when it becomes thin and rotten, then treat the area as needed, and finish with the abscess as we have discussed; and extract the blood or moisture you find, then treat the area as needed, and close the area.
dou chancre	Of ulcer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have discussed in the division the characteristics of ulcer, and how one should proceed with medicines, and how one should avoid the use of iron; and we say that ulcer appears on the womb, and much caution is required in its treatment, and the ancients said that when an ulcer is in a place where it can be cut away, as with an ulcer on the breasts, on the thigh, and in similar places, it should be completely removed when it is in its beginning; and when it is large and old, you should by no means approach it, for I was never able to cure any, nor did anyone cure any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the procedure, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you sometimes purge the patient of black bile; then bleed him if he has clear repletion, then prepare a suitable place for the patient to undergo the procedure; then apply your hooks to the ulcer, and remove it from all sides, and take it out from all sides without leaving anything; and let the blood flow fully, and press well on the area with your hand or with something else, and if the bleeding from the incision in the artery or the vein troubles you, then cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then treat it with further care until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose;  donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance;  et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already spoken in the division of the types of dropsy, and in what way the accumulation of water is formed, and the signs of each type, and the cure that is done by medicines, and that which is cured by the use of iron: this applies only to ascites; and one should not use iron on these two types: namely, tympanites and hypochondriac dropsy, for it is a deadly matter. Therefore, when you treat this type of dropsy called “ascites” with medicines, and if the cure does not help, then observe whether the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as fever and bowel looseness and similar issues; in such cases do not use iron, for there is danger in it. But if you see the patient is of strong vitality, and he has no illness other than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should proceed as follows: lift the patient upright with your hands, and the assistant presses the abdomen to push the water to the lowest part of the chest, then take the pointed trocar in this way:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let it be sharp on two sides.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	with a point, yet not so penetrating that it could reach the intestine when inserted and injure it; then observe if the dropsy has developed towards the intestines: if so, you must make an incision on the belly three fingers' width below the wrist; and if the dropsy is due to disease of the liver, let your incision be on the left of the belly by three fingers' width; and if it is from the spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary for the patient to lie on the incision so that the excess fluids do not flow into that weak spot; then pierce the skin with the instrument, insert it, and raise your hand with the spatula between the skin and the membrane as if skimming by the size of a fingernail or slightly around it; then pierce the membrane until the spatula reaches the empty space, and that is where the water is, then draw it out, and insert this instrument here, which has the following shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it resembles a delicate silver tube, made of brass or light bronze, with a small hole at the bottom part; and on one side, three holes; on another side, two holes; and one hole on the remaining side; the head is shaped like a pen, which is the form of incision that scribes make to cut the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	at the top is the small handle, so that when the instrument reaches the water, it descends immediately on the instrument; then empty it by half or a third, for if you empty more than necessary at that moment, the patient may die from the dissipation of his life’s spirit, or he may faint, or approach death; but empty it according to the measure of his strength, and according to what his condition, his strength, and his pulse indicate; then withdraw the instrument and retain the water, and it is held back now by the stopper that blocks the hole in the membrane, as I have mentioned, that you pierce in this way; then reapply the instrument the next day, if you see the patient tolerating it, and draw out a small amount of water; do this for several days, and be careful not to overdo it so that only a small amount of water remains.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you have doubts about the patient, and you leave a lot of water in him, treat him with hot sand or a hot grave, and with much sweating, or baths, and in the sun, and forbid him from drinking; and treat him with drying medicines until he is healed, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and the spleen after the extraction of the water, as I mentioned before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Sometimes children are born who have no opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in the proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	It is therefore necessary immediately to pierce it with a very fine spatula in this way:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place in the opening a fine lead nail, tie it, and keep it there for three or four days, and when he wishes to urinate, remove the nail, let him urinate, and then replace it; sometimes this may not be necessary, as the passing urine will keep it from closing.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	For those whose opening is small, let it be treated with the lead nail as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those whose opening is not in the correct place are afflicted, for some are born with the opening at the top of the penis, causing them to be unable to urinate forward unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot procreate because the semen cannot reach the womb, which is a serious condition.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of the operation is such that the patient should often lie on his back, then extend the head of the penis and cut it as one would cut a pen, so that the opening is in the middle, as it should be; take care to stop any bleeding that often occurs, and if it does, stop it with something that stops bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	Of pustules on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often these pustules appear on the penis, and are an appearance of unsightly flesh; some are malignant, some are not; you should grasp them with a fine hook, cut and clean them all, then apply cotton moistened with Egyptian ointment; then treat it with diafinicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the pustule is malignant, foul in color and odor, you must apply cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it, and if the pustule is on top of the penis, with part of it under the skin and part of it on the outside, you must first remove the part that is inside; and when it has healed, then treat the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it all at once, there is no guarantee that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and blackening and decay may appear on the penis and in the testicles; you must therefore remove all that is blackened and decayed, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate peel and vetch, and then continue with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if a blood flow comes, apply the lunar cautery in this manner:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery aids in two conditions simultaneously: namely, to stop blood flow, and to address decay; and if the head of the penis is corrupted and contracted, you must insert a lead tube into the canal of the penis, and let the patient urinate through it; and when the skin thickens at the head of the penis, which happens in those who have not been circumcised, or it occurs due to wound or abscess, you must then peel it back with a sharp instrument, until the binding is released, and the head of the penis is freed on all sides; and if this is difficult to accomplish, you must peel it back with a spatula slightly from the head of the penis and the skin; then gently separate the two, and place a fine linen cloth soaked in cold water so that it does not thicken again.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a separation of continuous tissue like other wounds; however, when we perform this procedure by our own decision, especially on children, it is necessary to perform it in the best, safest, and least painful way possible.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach circumcision for their children, as it was not practiced in their laws, and we only have knowledge of it through our own experiments.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most practitioners and healers perform circumcision using a small blade, with forceps and sometimes a razor; but the tissue retracts, as there are two layers, and sometimes they cut only the top layer while leaving the lower layer intact.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Then it becomes necessary to cut again, causing double pain, and during the cleaning with the blade, the member’s tip is not securely held; while cleaning with the fingernail, the instrument may slip, worsening the procedure, and at times, there is no need for cleaning at all, as I have seen.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	I have found a better method using forceps and tying with thread, as the forceps cut equally well on both the upper and lower parts.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press with your hand, the tool cuts evenly in one smooth motion; but make sure the thread is tightly secured around the skin. First, prepare the child, if they understand, to think you are only tying thread around the penis; then distract them in every way you can. Next, stand the child between your hands so they remain upright, and hide the forceps and instruments in your hands or under your feet so the child doesn’t see them. Then grasp the penis, blow on the tip, and pull it up until the head of the penis is visible. Clean it thoroughly of any dirt gathered there, then secure it with a double thread, then tie another knot below, slightly lower, with another thread. Hold it between two fingers by the second knot, with your thumb and index finger, and cut between the two knots. Then quickly remove the upper knot and pull the head of the penis. Allow the blood to flow slowly, as this is beneficial. Then apply powder, and on the powder place a cloth coated with the white of a boiled egg mixed with rosewater and fresh rose oil, and leave it in place until the next day. Continue with further treatment until it heals.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The design of the forceps for the cleaning is as follows: the two heads should be thin and sharp, and the heads should be as wide as the handle evenly.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	An error in the procedure occurs if the inner tissue retracts from the incision; in such a case, you must extend it with your fingernail before the area becomes infected, and cut it evenly. If you can’t hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with forceps and cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If three days pass and the area below the penis swells, leave it until the hot swelling has subsided, then lightly peel the skin; cut it as best you can, taking care not to harm the penis itself, as this will cause no harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the area with substances that close wounds in powder form, as we discussed in the section on powders, and if you cut more of the tissue than necessary and it extends beyond, this will not cause harm; treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	On the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to obstruction by stone, or clotted blood, or mucus, or fleshy growth, or similar things, as we have stated in the section; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is caused by a stone located at the neck of the bladder, the patient must bend over on their knees, place their feet on their back, extend their abdomen over the back, and hold their breath as much as possible; then the neck of the bladder is compressed to force the stone upwards, by which the urine is released; and if it does not come, as we said, and the patient feels great pain, you must use the extraction instrument called the "syringe," whose form is as follows: it should be made of fine silver with a delicate feather-like tube, as from a bird’s feather; and the tube should be one and a half palms in length, with a fine tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the method for releasing the urine is that you take a doubled thread, tie a bit of wool or cotton at the end, and insert the end of the thread inside the syringe; then cut off the excess wool and insert it to the tip of the syringe, then coat the syringe with oil, butter, or egg white, and seat the patient on a chair, anointing the bladder and the penis with warm oil, olive oil, and warm water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis over at the loop; then push the syringe further until it reaches the bladder, and the patient will feel it reach the empty area, which is not done according to this order except because the duct through which it passes is twisted; then extend the thread with the wool bit by bit, and the urine will follow the wool, then remove it, and let the urine flow; and repeat with the syringe until the bladder is emptied and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	On the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When abrasions or blood appear in the bladder, or decay has gathered there, and you wish to distill waters and medicines into it, do so with the instrument called the "clepsydra," whose form is as follows:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is sealed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the capped end, where the medicine flows, should tightly stop the penis without addition, so that moisture can be drawn out and injected when needed; and when you want to pour your medicines into the bladder, place the end of the cup in the moisture, and pull on the plunger inside; this will draw the moisture into the cup, and then push the plunger firmly inside again; this will let the moisture flow in, and it will reach the bladder immediately, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the fine clyster used for the bladder: it is here.
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is made of silver or brass, and the head is higher; and below is a ring where the cord is attached; then take a sheep's bladder and put in it the moisture with which you wish to cleanse the bladder, then tie it firmly between the two rings with good, double thread, and heat that moisture slightly over the fire; then insert the head of the clyster into the penis, then press your hand over the bladder with the moisture gradually, until the patient feels that this moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don’t have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, make a circle from it, and pierce it roundly all around; then insert a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle as you would a drum, and put inside whatever oil, moisture, and water you desire, and tie it to the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	On stones
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken in the section about the types of stones, and the extraction together with medicines; and I have explained the difference between stones formed in the kidneys, with all signs, and in which stones one must operate by incision; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder appears most often in children, and the sign is that liquid flows from the bladder, appearing as water in its subtlety; and sand appears in it, and the patient scratches his penis, which sometimes hangs limp, and then stiffens; and many such flows come from the rectum; and treatment is easy in children until they are four years old, and very difficult in the elderly, and moderate in young adults, those between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by clyster to remove all feces from the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For sometimes this blocks the way of reaching the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet, turn and move him from below, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and it sometimes leaves the upper place; then make him sit prepared between your hands, with his hands under his thighs, so that the bladder is inclined downward; then search for and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hasten now to cut over the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not settle entirely upon touching, moisten your index finger in oil on your left hand if the patient is a child, or your middle finger if the patient is a fully-grown young man; then insert it into his rectum, seek out the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press upwards with your finger, and push it outward to where you want to make the incision.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and instruct him to lift the testicles upwards with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin that is beneath the testicles in the area where the incision is made; then insert the cutting spatula, whose form is as follows:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make the incision between what lies between the testicles and the rectum, not in the middle but on the left buttock side; and place it straight over the stone, and your fingers should always be at the rectum, and the incision should be transversal so that it is wide on the outside, and narrow on the inside, according to the size of the stone, but not too large; by chance the finger pressing at the rectum may force it out without difficulty; and know that there are certain stones that have angles and edges: they are hard to remove; and some are smooth, like an acorn, and round, for which removal is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	For those with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not come out, you must grip it with tongs which are like a file at the tip, to better hold the stone so that it does not escape; or you may insert below it a fine instrument curved at the tip; and if you cannot manage to remove it this way, enlarge the opening a bit, and if there is excessive bleeding, stem it with vitriol; and if there is more than one stone, push the largest one first to the neck of the bladder, then cut over it, then pull it out, and remove the smaller ones afterward if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it must be cut up, and a larger wound must be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things may happen to the patient: either he dies, or the urine continues to flow where the place cannot heal; but nevertheless try to extract it, or to break it with the tongs, until you can pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon’s blood, and press it tightly, and place over it a cloth moistened with oil and wine, or with oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot swelling; then lay the patient back on his neck, and do not loosen the dressing until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen it, sprinkle the place well with oil and water, then treat it with dyafinicon ointment and basilicon ointment until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses appear in the wound along with corrosion, and clots of blood in the bladder, causing retention of urine, which is known by how blood flows with the urine: place your finger in the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrode and rot the bladder; then cleanse the wound with water, garlic, and salt, and assist it in all the ways you know, until it is healed; and each time you treat it, you must bind the two thighs together and apply medicines on the spot.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is lodged in the urethra and stuck inside, and the urine cannot exit, then treat it as I said earlier, if you can avoid the incision by this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tested this successfully.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take an iron drill in this form, with three angles fixed on a handle:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then insert the drill into the urethra gently, until it reaches the stone; and turn the drill with your hand little by little, until you can pierce the stone through; then the urine will immediately flow, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the urethra.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It will soon break, and will exit with the urine, and the patient will be healed; and if you cannot do this because of some obstacle, then tie a thread below the stone and another above it, then cut the penis at the stone between the two ties, then extract it, and untie the thread, and cleanse the clotted blood in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of stones in women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that stones form in women, and if it does happen, the treatment is difficult and avoided for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; the second is that a knowledgeable woman who would expose herself to doctors cannot be found, especially if she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.  Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;  et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third reason is that, perhaps, it is hard to find a woman skilled in this art with her hands; and the fourth reason is that the stone in women is deeper than in men, so a deeper incision is needed, which brings great fear. And if necessity demands it, you must take a well-informed midwife, though one is rarely found; and if you do not find one, then seek a chaste, skilled doctor, present her with a wise assistant familiar with women’s lives, or a woman who knows part of the art, and instruct her to do as you command for the stone's extraction; and examine very carefully if the woman is a virgin; if so, she should insert her finger into the anus and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she should press down on it with her finger and then insert her finger into the sick woman’s vagina, seeking and pressing with her left hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie;  et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it gradually from the bladder’s opening downward, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then she cuts over the stone at the thigh root, against the middle of the vagina, where it lies firmly, and feels the stone in that part;  and she must not move her finger from over or under the stone, and the incision should first be small; then insert the tool into the incision; if you feel the stone, widen the wound so that the stone can come out, knowing that there are many kinds of stones, such as small, large, rough, smooth, long, round, and those with roots.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Know these types to understand the extraction.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;  et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if blood overcomes you, apply crushed vitriol to the spot, holding it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your work, until the stone is extracted, and have the tools I told you for extracting stones from men to aid you in your work;  and if blood overcomes you, and it is from a cut artery, place powder on the spot and restrain it with tenting and bandages; do not persist further, and leave the stone unextracted, as the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided, and the place has calmed, return to your work until the stone is extracted.
de hernie carnouse	On fleshy hernias
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef;  et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous hernia is nothing more than an accumulation of moisture or white syfac beneath the heart of the testicles, which holds the egg; it is called “syfac,” and sometimes lies within the egg membrane, so that one thinks it is another egg;  and it is the skin of the testicle between the white syfac we mentioned; and this rarely happens.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the origin of this hernia is weakness that occurs in the testicles, and this substance is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;  et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it results from impact to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: yellowish, or blood red, or black, or watery white, and this is more common;  and these are the signs for identifying this mass, for if it is in the white syfac we mentioned, then the abscess is round, a bit long like the shape of an egg, and the testicle is not visible, as it is surrounded entirely by moisture.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the very tissue itself, then the abscess drains along with a part of the egg, and for this reason, it is thought that it is another kind of egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white membrane, one can feel it well; thus, when you wish to know the color of the moisture, test it with the small square instrument described above.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the instrument, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with a blade, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to his strength and the fullness of his body; then lay him on his back, on something slightly elevated, and place many cloths under him; then have him sit on his left side, and instruct the assistant to sit on his right, and to extend the penis to one of the two sides of the testicle sac; then take the spatumile leit (a small surgical instrument) and cut the skin of the testicle sac along its length to the area near the wrist, making a straight incision that divides the skin of the testicle sac down to the white membrane, and scrape it delicately as well as you can; then pierce the membrane filled with fluid with a large opening, and drain all the fluid, then apply your ointments, and stretch the membrane upwards; and do not touch the core of the testicles, but only the membrane; cut everything away or in small, precise pieces beside it delicately, because if you do not cut carefully, the fluid will return; and if the ‘egg’ moves away from your work, return it to its place when you have completed work on the membrane; then bring together the two edges of the testicle sac with a suture, then treat it as you would other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspensory, to prevent the flow of blood; then cut the testicle along with the suspensory vessel, and remove the egg, and treat it as we have described.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if fluid has gathered in two parts together, know that these are two branches; so cut the other part as you did the first, evenly, then wipe the blood, and place wool soaked in rose oil in the wound; and place other wool soaked in wine and oil outside, and put it on the two testicles, and place doubled cloths over it, and bind it with the bandage according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and fill them with shredded wool in this way, and they should be joined by stitching at the waistband of the trousers, and one of the ends should reach from the base to the back, and the other to the area of the wrist; and the other two ends to the two groins, and the entire restraint should be fastened at the belt of the trousers; and sometimes this branch is treated with cautery instead of with the blade, and it is that you take a thin cautery knife and cut the skin of the testicles, and it should be heated as we have said, so that the white membrane containing the fluid is uncovered; then take the cautery in this manner, and pierce that membrane with ointments, and scrape it with this thin, hot cautery knife:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And cut it in all the ways you can, until you have scraped it all out; and ensure that the heat does not touch the egg; and know that this procedure is safer; and take greater care to prevent the flow of blood than with the cutting procedure; and if anything goes wrong for you, or a hot abscess or flow of blood or anything else occurs, treat whatever is causing the issue according to what is previously described.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the patient is fearful and does not wish to undergo this procedure because of its horror, then administer perforation, as I tell you, and it is that when you are quite certain by the signs we have described that the watery branch is there, have the patient sit on a raised seat; then pierce the abscess on the lower part with a wide spatumile, and make the perforation along the length of the body; and let the opening be wide, so that all the fluid flows out; then put cotton on the spot, and bind it, and let the remainder of the fluid drain out, then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white membrane does not let the fluid out through the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a quill or the instrument used to draw fluid from dropsy patients, whose shape is described above; and enlarge the wound a bit, and know that the fluid will return, and it gathers again after about six months or thereabouts, and when it is gathered as before, thus will the patient pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the cutting of this branch, there is fear in many conditions, which is why it seems to me that it is often better to leave it; and I will tell you the procedure and appearances of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many abscesses come upon the body, and particularly upon the testicles; and it is due to many causes.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be understood as arising from sharp and bitter surplus fluid, which spreads to the testicles, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess is like the color of the body; and one finds no pain, and it is a severe abscess; and by chance, there is an abscess that is frightening, dangerous, and fiery in color, and sometimes it comes from an artery knot, or from vein swelling.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is due to an artery knot, it is known by the hot disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fingers; and it is not necessary to touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	The one that is caused by vein swelling is known by its feel when touched with the fingers, and one can well make an incision on this form, and on other flesh; and it is that you cut the core of the testicles, then lift the egg up, and pull it out from the white membrane, and free the suspensory from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the egg is already bound with its attached flesh, then you must pull out the egg and cut it; and if it is attached to the membrane or to what is within the vessels, you must free all that membrane and cut it circularly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the flesh’s growth is in the area behind, then you must cut it all out and extract the egg, as we have described.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your procedure is complete, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped in a wrapping like a bud, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient is greatly troubled when he walks; and the treatment of this condition is almost as dangerous as the one before, and yet we will describe the procedure for it, according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then press down the suspensory of the testicles with your fingers, along with the vessels that are near the penis, and the master should hold them and stretch them firmly; then cut with the broad cutting spatumile across, directly over the vessels, until they are exposed, and then scrape on each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries in the temples; then insert a needle with a doubled thread and tie it at the first place where the swelling has appeared, and tie it again at the other end; then cut them in the middle, straight along the length of the body, and draw out the corrupted fluids; then treat the wound as with others where swelling occurs, so that any vessels that nourish one of the testicles fall away; for through this, no harm will come, and if life flows to all the vessels, it is necessary to draw the testicles along with all the vessels; so that the bone does not lose its nourishment from the cutting of the vessels, and they dry out and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the membrane
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The occurrence of this condition is due to a tear that appears in the membrane, or an extension on the belly in the area of the groin, because of which the intestines descend from this rupture to one of the testicles; and this rupture is either of the membrane itself or of its extension, and these two types arise from many causes: either from a blow, or a jump, or straining, or lifting a heavy load, and similar things; and the signs, when it is an extension of the membrane, are that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscess is even down to the depth, because the membrane presses on the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign, when it is a tear in the membrane, is that it causes sudden pain at the onset, and the abscess appears uneven, just beneath the skin, and this is due to the protrusion of the intestine and the body outside the membrane.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And sometimes the omentum descends with the intestine, and it remains trapped there, causing the patient to suffer great pain, especially when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with a blade, there is danger, which is why it must be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the operation is as follows: command the patient to push the intestine back into the wound by hand if he can manage it; then support him under the neck with your hands, and raise his thighs; then stretch the heart above, and cut all along the skin of the testicles; then insert the lips of the incision using hooks as necessary to open the wound, so that the bone may come out; then peel back the fascia that is under the skin of the testicles, until the hard white fascia is fully exposed; then put your index finger in the part that surrounds the testicle, between the white fascia that is under the skin of the egg, and between the second fascia, and separate what is behind the egg and between the second fascia; then move with your right hand within the heart of the testicles, and hold up the white fascia with your left hand, and raise the egg with all the fascia towards the cut; then instruct the assistant to hold the egg upward and untie what is left behind the ligation; and search with your fingers if any part of the intestine is caught within the hard white fascia, and if you find anything, push it down into the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made of ten strands, and put it in the back part of the fascia, which is beyond the skin of the testicles; after the cut, then cut off the ends of the threads until there are four strands; then assemble them one over the other in the form of a cross, and tie the fascia, which we have said is under the skin of the testicles, with a strong tie in two places;
